         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <h1 name="d4ba" id="d4ba" class="graf graf--h3 graf--leading graf--title">Standing on the shoulders of Giants?—?Node.js, Vue 2, Stripe, Heroku and Amazon&nbsp;S3</h1>
           <blockquote name="831e" id="831e" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--h3 graf--trailing">
            This post goes through building a website for selling products. We set up a Vue client side application and Node.js server side app. The apps use Stripe’s Javascript libraries for payment processing. We deploy the client app to Amazon S3 and deploy the Node.js server to the cloud using Heroku.
           </blockquote>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section name="1a73" class="section section--body">
         <div class="section-divider">
          <hr class="section-divider">
         </div>
         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <p name="1231" id="1231" class="graf graf--p graf--leading">In this tutorial we are going to build a website for selling artisan bundles of sticks online. It is going to be called <a href="http://stickly.io/#/" data-href="http://stickly.io/#/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Stickly</strong></a>! In order to make this site we’re going to need a Product display page, an Order page and a Confirmation details page. We’ll accept payments using Stripe’s client side and server side Javascript libraries.</p>
           <figure name="00b6" id="00b6" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 306px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 43.8%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png" data-width="1200" data-height="525" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figcaption class="imageCaption">
             Screenshot of finished landing page for&nbsp;Stickly
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
           <p name="6509" id="6509" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">To build the frontend we’ll use Vue 2 with <a href="https://github.com/vuejs/vue-router" data-href="https://github.com/vuejs/vue-router" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">vue-router</a> for client side routing. The frontend application will be responsible for collecting user information and sending a request to Stripe for a special token. Once we have that token from Stripe, our client side code will forward the token to our server in order to initiate the charge.</p>
           <p name="a1f6" id="a1f6" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The server will be made from Node.js using express and its associated utility libraries. There will be two endpoints. One for creating a new charge and the other for returning details about a particular charge, based on a unique identifier that we get from Stripe.</p>
           <p name="c213" id="c213" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">In order to build this application and start selling online, we are going to utilize third party services. To build a real world website that accept actual payments on the internet you’ll need to sign up for the following services and locate your special API keys.</p>
           <figure name="962f" id="962f" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 350px;">

              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*m6pXBFDNitef-VSsgbWC2g.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*m6pXBFDNitef-VSsgbWC2g.png">

           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="4521" id="4521" class="graf graf--li graf-after--figure"><a href="https://stripe.com/" data-href="https://stripe.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Stripe</a>: Stripe is the current standard for developers accepting payments in the US. There are many competitors out there but Stripe’s extensive documentation and ease of use has made it the de facto choice for payment processing online. We are going to use their [client side](<a href="https://stripe.com/docs/stripe.js" data-href="https://stripe.com/docs/stripe.js" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://stripe.com/docs/stripe.js</a>?) Javascript library and their server side [Node.js package](<a href="https://stripe.com/docs/api/node" data-href="https://stripe.com/docs/api/node" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://stripe.com/docs/api/node</a>).</li>
           </ul>

It simplifies the task of deploying and maintaining cloud infrastructure.            </ul>
           <h3 name="5aa9" id="5aa9" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--li">Frontend Application</h3>
           <p name="1d90" id="1d90" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">First we are going to build the frontend Vue.js application. This is the website portion that the user will see. Ultimately it will be hosted using Amazon S3, but first we have to set everything up.</p>
           <p name="d5c5" id="d5c5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The Vue.js core team maintains a collection of generators for scaffolding new projects. For this tutorial we are going to use the <a href="https://github.com/vuejs-templates/webpack-simple" data-href="https://github.com/vuejs-templates/webpack-simple" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">webpack-simple template</a> to quickly get a client side Vue.js up and running. This will include a custom Webpack setup and specific `.vue` files that contain our HTML, CSS and Javascript for dedicated components.</p>
           <p name="941d" id="941d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you have not used Vue before you are in for a treat! If you are experienced with Vue this setup should be very straightforward to you.</p>
           <p name="d010" id="d010" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We are going to use <a href="http://bulma.io/" data-href="http://bulma.io/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Bulma</a> for styling, which is a Flexbox based CSS library. If you are new to using CSS Flexbox you can check out the Scotch.io article <a href="https://scotch.io/tutorials/a-visual-guide-to-css3-flexbox-properties" data-href="https://scotch.io/tutorials/a-visual-guide-to-css3-flexbox-properties" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>. In depth knowledge of Flexbox is not a prerequisite for this tutorial.</p>
           <h4 name="d105" id="d105" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Create the Vue.js&nbsp;app</h4>
           <p name="c2ee" id="c2ee" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Create the Vue.js static website app with the following commands in your command line interface.</p>
           <pre name="5d8c" id="5d8c" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ vue init webpack-simple YOUR_APP_NAME<br>$ cd YOUR_APP_NAME<br>$ npm install<br>$ npm install vue-router moment — save</pre>
           <p name="3e63" id="3e63" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">This generates our new project and includes the additional dependecies for client side routing and date formating.</p>
           <h4 name="0438" id="0438" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Instantiate the application</h4>
           <p name="c6c9" id="c6c9" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Our <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">src/main.js</strong> file is going to be the nerve center for our application. This is the first file to get called and it will call all of our components and link our Javascript application to the index.html page. Let’s import all of the components, libraries and setup we need for our application within this file.</p>
           <p name="e326" id="e326" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/main.js</strong></p>
           <pre name="cc28" id="cc28" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">// Environment configuration<br>if (process.env.NODE_ENV === ‘production’) {<br> window.endpoint = ‘<a href="https://stickly.herokuapp.com%27" data-href="https://stickly.herokuapp.com'" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://stickly.herokuapp.com'</a>;<br>} else {<br> window.endpoint = ‘<a href="http://localhost:3000%27" data-href="http://localhost:3000'" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">http://localhost:3000'</a>;<br>}</pre>
           <pre name="3f18" id="3f18" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Global Variables<br>window.moment = require(‘moment’);<br>window.axios = require(‘axios’);<br>window.axios.defaults.headers.common[‘X-Requested-With’] = ‘XMLHttpRequest’;</pre>
           <pre name="3713" id="3713" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">import Vue from ‘vue’<br>import VueRouter from ‘vue-router’<br>import App from ‘./components/App.vue’<br>import Product from ‘./components/Product.vue’<br>import Order from ‘./components/Order.vue’<br>import Complete from ‘./components/Complete.vue’</pre>
           <pre name="144c" id="144c" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">Vue.use(VueRouter);</pre>
           <pre name="5231" id="5231" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Register routes<br>const routes = [<br> { name: ‘home’, path: ‘/’, component: Product },<br> { name: ‘order’, path: ‘/order’, component: Order },<br> { name: ‘order-complete’, path: ‘/order-complete/:id’, component: Complete }<br>];</pre>
           <pre name="0e81" id="0e81" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">const router = new VueRouter({<br> routes<br>});</pre>
           <pre name="7dc2" id="7dc2" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Instantiate application to the DOM<br>new Vue({<br> router,<br> el: ‘#app’,<br> data(){<br>     return {};<br> },<br> render: h =&gt; h(App)<br>});</pre>
           <p name="a1a8" id="a1a8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">The first thing we do here is determine whether we are in our production or development environment. This value will be set by webpack when we run `npm run dev` (for development) or `npm run build` (for production). Based on the environment we set a global variable attached to the browser’s window object that determines which URL our Vue app will make XHR (ajax) requests to. For making asynchronous requests from the background we are going to use <a href="https://github.com/mzabriskie/axios" data-href="https://github.com/mzabriskie/axios" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">axios</a>.</p>
           <p name="2609" id="2609" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Next we register the components we will need and bind them to specific routes. This is the pattern required for setting up client side routing with <a href="https://github.com/vuejs/vue-router" data-href="https://github.com/vuejs/vue-router" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">vue-router</a>, the official Vue.js routing package maintained by the Vue.js core team.</p>
           <p name="2806" id="2806" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We will also need to modify our <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">index.html</em> page to include the Stripe javascript library, the Bulma CSS framework, style classes and Font Awesome.</p>
           <p name="a131" id="a131" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./index.html</strong></p>
           <pre name="546f" id="546f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;<br>&lt;html lang=”en”&gt;<br>&lt;head&gt;<br> &lt;meta charset=”utf-8"&gt;<br> &lt;meta http-equiv=”X-UA-Compatible” content=”IE=edge”&gt;<br> &lt;meta name=”viewport” content=”width=device-width, initial-scale=1"&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="ae9b" id="ae9b" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;title&gt;Stickly&lt;/title&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="a745" id="a745" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;!-- Styles --&gt;<br> &lt;link rel=’stylesheet’ href=’<a href="https://maxcdn.bootstrapcdn.com/font-awesome/4.7.0/css/font-awesome.min.css%27" data-href="https://maxcdn.bootstrapcdn.com/font-awesome/4.7.0/css/font-awesome.min.css'" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://maxcdn.bootstrapcdn.com/font-awesome/4.7.0/css/font-awesome.min.css'</a>&gt;<br> &lt;link rel=”stylesheet” href=”<a href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/bulma/0.5.1/css/bulma.css" data-href="https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/bulma/0.5.1/css/bulma.css" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/bulma/0.5.1/css/bulma.css</a>"&gt;<br> &lt;link rel=”stylesheet” href=”./css/main.css”&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="c6e2" id="c6e2" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;/head&gt;<br>&lt;body&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”hero is-fullheight”&gt;<br> &lt;div id=’app’&gt;&lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="bcbb" id="bcbb" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;!-- Scripts --&gt;<br> &lt;script type=”text/javascript” src=”<a href="https://js.stripe.com/v2/" data-href="https://js.stripe.com/v2/" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://js.stripe.com/v2/</a>"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;<br> &lt;script src=”/dist/build.js”&gt;&lt;/script&gt;<br>&lt;/body&gt;<br>&lt;/html&gt;</pre>
           <p name="8734" id="8734" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Our Vue.js application will be bound to <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">index.html</em> through the “app” id tag where it will mount our App component. This app component will display most of our content and our Vue.js application logic. It displays a navigation section and the special `&lt;router-view&gt;&lt;/router-view&gt;` component. This component tells vue-router where to mount our views. The router takes the current URL and mounts the component to this space accordingly.</p>
           <p name="d857" id="d857" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/components/App.vue</strong></p>
           <pre name="6031" id="6031" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;template&gt;<br> &lt;div id=”app”&gt;<br> &lt;!-- Nav --&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”hero-head”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”container”&gt;<br> &lt;nav class=”nav”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”container”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”nav-left”&gt;<br> &lt;router-link to=”/” class=”nav-item”&gt;Stickly&lt;/router-link&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”nav-toggle”&gt;<br> &lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”nav-right nav-menu”&gt;<br> &lt;a class=”nav-item” href=’<a href="mailto:support@stickly.com" data-href="mailto:support@stickly.com" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">support@stickly.com</a>’&gt;<br> Contact<br> &lt;/a&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/nav&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="f03b" id="f03b" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">  &lt;router-view&gt;&lt;/router-view&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/template&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="ddad" id="ddad" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;script&gt;<br>export default {<br> name: ‘app’,<br> data () {<br> return {}<br> }<br>}<br>&lt;/script&gt;</pre>
           <p name="03e4" id="03e4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">The App componet is the heart of our application. All of our other Vue components will render where the router-view component is. This way we do not need to duplicate code for the Nav bar or HTML headers on every page.</p>
           <p name="996b" id="996b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We defined in our *main.js* file that when the user hits the root of our application the Product component should render. Let’s define that now!</p>
           <h4 name="654c" id="654c" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Create the Product&nbsp;page</h4>
           <p name="e20e" id="e20e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">The product page is the landing page that entices the user to buy our product, in this case a bundle of sticks. There is an open source template called <a href="https://github.com/dansup/bulma-templates" data-href="https://github.com/dansup/bulma-templates" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">dansup/bulma-templates</a> that we can use to quickly style the product page. There are lots of example templates for Bulma that you can browse [<a href="https://dansup.github.io/bulma-templates/" data-href="https://dansup.github.io/bulma-templates/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>]() and <a href="http://bulma.io/expo/" data-href="http://bulma.io/expo/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>, depending on what you are building. The product page template is a good starting point, though I have made some minor modifications.</p>
           <figure name="c724" id="c724" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 306px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 43.8%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png" data-width="1200" data-height="525" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">

               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*PT1xCy5RlAMG2Q-oDaR5mA.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="2508" id="2508" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/components/Product.vue</strong></p>
           <pre name="165e" id="165e" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;template&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”section”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”container”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”columns” style=’min-height:800px;’&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”column is-6"&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”image is-2by2"&gt;<br> &lt;img src=”<a href="https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg" data-href="https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg</a>”&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”column is-5 is-offset-1"&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”title is-2"&gt;Bundle of Sticks&lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;p class=”title is-3 has-text-muted”&gt;$ 15&lt;/p&gt;<br> &lt;hr&gt;<br> &lt;br&gt;<br> &lt;p&gt;This bundle of sticks provides an earthy fragrance and aesthetic natural appeal. Your bundle of sticks will come with a personalized note. The perfect natural gift for any time of year!&lt;/p&gt;<br> &lt;br&gt;<br> &lt;br&gt;<br> &lt;p class=’level’&gt;<br> &lt;router-link to=”/order” class=”button is-large is-primary level-item has-text-centered”&gt;Buy Now&lt;/router-link&gt;<br> &lt;/p&gt;<br> &lt;br&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/template&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="966d" id="966d" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;script&gt;<br>export default {}<br>&lt;/script&gt;</pre>
           <p name="ffef" id="ffef" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">As you can see this component is all plain HTML with Bulma’s specific classes for styling. The only Vue specific part of this file is the `&lt;router-link&gt;&lt;/router-link&gt;` component. This automatically generates an anchor tag and connects the route to the routes we defined for vue-router in our *main.js* file.</p>
           <p name="3633" id="3633" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">When the user clicks the Order Now button they will be redirected to the Order page where they can fill out their details and submit their information for payment processing.</p>
           <h4 name="c7a5" id="c7a5" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">The Order&nbsp;page</h4>
           <p name="385d" id="385d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">The order page displays fields for the user’s contact details (name and email), their shipping information, a personalized note for the bundle of sticks and fields for their credit card details. Additionally, we do checks to make sure that the credit card fields are filled out correctly with some Vue.js form validation techniques in the `validate` method.</p>
           <p name="891f" id="891f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/components/Order.vue</strong> (the html portion)</p>
           <pre name="6405" id="6405" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;template&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’container’&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’columns’&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’column is-4'&gt;<br> &lt;img src=”<a href="https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg" data-href="https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://cdn.scotch.io/2842/b7yhhuUPSGO1fEkMHD6P_sticks.jpeg</a>" alt=”A bundle of sticks”&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’column is-4'&gt; <br> &lt;div class=’field’&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;Name&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”control has-icons-left has-icons-right”&gt;<br> &lt;input class=”input” type=”text” placeholder=”First and Last” v-model=’name’&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”icon is-small is-left”&gt;<br> &lt;i class=”fa fa-user”&gt;&lt;/i&gt;<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;Email&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”control has-icons-left has-icons-right”&gt;<br> &lt;input class=”input” type=”text” placeholder=”Email address” v-model=’email’&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”icon is-small is-left”&gt;<br> &lt;i class=”fa fa-envelope”&gt;&lt;/i&gt;<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="b499" id="b499" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre"> &lt;hr id=’left-line’&gt;<br> <br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label for=”card_number”&gt;Card Number&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input id=”card_number” v-model=”card.number” type=”text” :class=”[‘is-danger’ ? cardNumberError : ‘’, ‘input’]” placeholder=’4242424242424242'&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”help is-danger” v-show=”cardNumberError”&gt;<br> {{ cardNumberError }}<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="bbd1" id="bbd1" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label for=”cvc”&gt;CVC&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input id=”cvc” v-model=”card.cvc” type=”text” class=”input” placeholder=’123'&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”help is-danger” v-show=”cardCvcError”&gt;<br> {{ cardCvcError }}<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="b041" id="b041" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label for=”exp_month”&gt;Expiry Month&lt;/label&gt;<br> <br> &lt;input id=”exp_month” v-model=”card.exp_month” type=”text” :class=”[‘is-danger’ ? cardMonthError : ‘’, ‘input’]” placeholder=”MM”&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”help is-danger” v-show=”cardMonthError”&gt;<br> {{ cardMonthError }}<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="8c37" id="8c37" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label for=”exp_month”&gt;Expiry Year&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input id=”exp_year” v-model=”card.exp_year” type=”text” :class=”[‘is-danger’ ? cardYearError : ‘’, ‘input’]” placeholder=”YY”&gt;<br> &lt;span class=”help is-danger” v-show=”cardYearError”&gt;<br> {{ cardYearError }}<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> <br> &lt;div class=”help is-danger” v-if=”cardCheckError”&gt;<br> &lt;span&gt;{{ cardCheckErrorMessage }}&lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt; <br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’column is-4'&gt; <br> &lt;label&gt;Special Note&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;textarea class=”textarea” placeholder=”What would you like the note to say?” v-model=’specialNote’&gt;&lt;/textarea&gt;<br> <br> &lt;hr&gt;<br> <br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;Address&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input type=’text’ class=’input’ v-model=’address.street’ placeholder=’123 Fake St #303'&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;City&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input type=’text’ class=’input’ v-model=’address.city’ placeholder=’San Francisco’&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;State&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input type=’text’ class=’input’ v-model=’address.state’ placeholder=’CA’&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”field”&gt;<br> &lt;label&gt;Zip&lt;/label&gt;<br> &lt;input type=’text’ class=’input’ v-model=’address.zip’ placeholder=’94607'&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;div class=”columns”&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’column is-12'&gt;<br> &lt;button type=”submit” class=”button is-primary is-large is-pulled-right” <a href="http://twitter.com/click" data-href="http://twitter.com/click" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" title="Twitter profile for @click" rel="noopener" target="_blank">@click</a>.prevent=”validate” :disabled=”cardCheckSending”&gt;<br> &lt;span v-if=”cardCheckSending”&gt;<br> &lt;i class=”fa fa-btn fa-spinner fa-spin”&gt;&lt;/i&gt; <br> Ordering…<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;span v-else&gt;<br> Place Order<br> &lt;/span&gt;<br> &lt;/button&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/template&gt;<br>&lt;style&gt;<br>h2 { text-decoration: underline; }<br>.textarea:not([rows]) { max-height: 110px; min-height: 110px; }<br>.container { margin-bottom: 30px; }<br>.column &gt; img { margin-top: 60px; }<br>.button-field { display: flex; justify-content: center; }<br>#left-line { margin-top:27px; }<br>&lt;/style&gt;</pre>
           <blockquote name="d4b5" id="d4b5" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--pre">
            <strong class="markup--strong markup--blockquote-strong">Update: </strong>There is also the 
            <a href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements" data-href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">vue-stripe-elements</a> component that can abstract away a lot of this code by utilizing Stripe’s prebuilt 
            <a href="https://stripe.com/docs/elements" data-href="https://stripe.com/docs/elements" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Elements</a>.
           </blockquote>
           <p name="5430" id="5430" class="graf graf--p graf-after--blockquote">In the above template code we style the page and provide an image of the product the customer is about to buy. Additionally, we bind the input for these form fields using `v-model`. We’ll have to define these fields in the vue object’s data property, featured below. We also provide helper classes bound to specific properties to show red error messages when forms are not filled out properly or left blank.</p>
           <p name="e78f" id="e78f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The Javascript logic for this component lives in the same portion and is featured below. This code is responsible for binding data to the form fields, obtaining a token from Stripe and sending the payment request to our Node.js server.</p>
           <p name="9da8" id="9da8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/components/Order.vue</strong> (the JS portion)</p>
           <pre name="8671" id="8671" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;script&gt;<br>import axios from ‘axios’;</pre>
           <pre name="a452" id="a452" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">export default {<br> data(){<br>  return {<br>   stripeKey: ‘YOUR_STRIPE_PUBLIC_KEY’,</pre>
           <pre name="bb40" id="bb40" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// fields<br>   name: ‘Connor Leech’,<br>   email: ‘<a href="mailto:connor@employbl.com" data-href="mailto:connor@employbl.com" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">connor@employbl.com</a>’,<br>   specialNote: ‘This is the text to put on the bundle of sticks’,<br>   address: {<br>     street: ‘123 Something Lane’,<br>     city: ‘San Francisco’,<br>     state: ‘CA’,<br>     zip: ‘94607’<br>   },<br>   card: {<br>     number: ‘4242424242424242’,<br>     cvc: ‘123’,<br>     exp_month: ‘01’,<br>     exp_year: ‘19’<br>   },<br>   // validation<br>   cardNumberError: null,<br>   cardCvcError: null,<br>   cardMonthError: null,<br>   cardYearError: null,<br>   cardCheckSending: false,<br>   cardCheckError: false,<br>   cardCheckErrorMessage: ‘’<br>  }<br> },<br> methods: {<br>   validate(){<br>     this.clearCardErrors();<br>     let valid = true;<br>     if(!this.card.number){ valid = false; this.cardNumberError = “Card Number is Required”; }<br>     if(!this.card.cvc){ valid = false; this.cardCvcError = “CVC is Required”; }<br>     if(!this.card.exp_month){ valid = false; this.cardMonthError = “Month is Required”; }<br>     if(!this.card.exp_year){ valid = false; this.cardYearError = “Year is Required”; }<br>     if(valid){<br>       this.createToken();<br>     }<br>   },<br>   clearCardErrors(){<br>     this.cardNumberError = null;<br>     this.cardCvcError = null;<br>     this.cardMonthError = null;<br>     this.cardYearError = null;<br>   },<br>   createToken() {<br>     this.cardCheckError = false;<br>     window.Stripe.setPublishableKey(this.stripeKey);<br>     window.Stripe.createToken(this.card, $.proxy(this.stripeResponseHandler, this));<br>     this.cardCheckSending = true;<br>   },<br>   stripeResponseHandler(status, response) {<br>     this.cardCheckSending = false;<br>     if (response.error) {<br>       this.cardCheckErrorMessage = response.error.message;<br>       this.cardCheckError = true;<br>       console.error(response.error);<br>     } else {<br>       // token to create a charge on our server <br>       var token_from_stripe = response.id;<br>       var request = {<br>         name: this.name,<br>         email: this.email,<br>         specialNote: this.specialNote,<br>         address: this.address,<br>         card: this.card,<br>         token_from_stripe: token_from_stripe<br>       };</pre>
           <pre name="837f" id="837f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">       // Send to our server<br>       axios.post(`${window.endpoint}/charge`, request)<br>         .then((res) =&gt; {<br>           var error = res.data.error;<br>           var charge = res.data.charge;<br>           if (error){<br>             console.error(error);<br>           } else {<br>             this.$router.push({ path: `order-complete/${charge.id}` })<br>           }<br>       });<br>     }<br>   }<br> }<br>}<br>&lt;/script&gt;</pre>
           <blockquote name="216d" id="216d" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--pre">
            <strong class="markup--strong markup--blockquote-strong">Update again: </strong>Looking back on this code I would probably rewrite it using 
            <a href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements" data-href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">vue-stripe-elements</a>. Originally I had an issue getting it set up but merged 
            <a href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements/pull/9" data-href="https://github.com/fromAtoB/vue-stripe-elements/pull/9" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">a PR</a> with some getting started instructions to make everything crystal clear
           </blockquote>
           <p name="b725" id="b725" class="graf graf--p graf-after--blockquote">The `createToken()` function uses the Stripe.js library to create a unique token for our particular charge request. Once we have that token, we trigger the `stripeResponseHandler` method. This checks that there are no errors and submits the request to our server for processing. If we successfully make a charge on our Node.js server using the token provided to us by Stripe.js we redirect the user to the Order Complete page. There is additional logic here for rendering the validation errors as well.</p>
           <h4 name="99d5" id="99d5" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Order Complete&nbsp;page</h4>
           <p name="0845" id="0845" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">And finally, we get to the order complete page. This page will be rendered after we successfully create the charge on our server. The URL will include a unique id associated with the particular charge we created. This URL will be persistent so the user can browse back to it at any time in order to view their order details.</p>
           <p name="33e9" id="33e9" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./src/components/Complete.vue</strong></p>
           <pre name="de6b" id="de6b" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;template&gt;<br> &lt;div class=’container content’&gt;<br> &lt;br&gt;<br> &lt;h3 style=’color: white;’&gt;Order complete!&lt;/h3&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="7f5f" id="7f5f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre"> &lt;p&gt;Congratulations! Your order for Sticks will be shipped out within 1–2 business days. &lt;a href=’’&gt;<a href="mailto:support@stickly.com" data-href="mailto:support@stickly.com" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">support@stickly.com</a>&lt;/a&gt;. We sent you a confirmation email for your records. Thanks so much!&lt;/p&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="d813" id="d813" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;div v-if=’orderDetails’&gt;<br> &lt;dl&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Order Number&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.id }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Order Created&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.created | moment }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Payment Amount&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.amount | currency }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Shipping Address&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.shipping.address.line1 }}, {{ orderDetails.shipping.address.city }}, {{ orderDetails.shipping.address.state }} {{ orderDetails.shipping.address.postal_code }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Engraving Text&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.description }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;dt&gt;Email&lt;/dt&gt;<br> &lt;dd&gt;{{ orderDetails.receipt_email }}&lt;/dd&gt;<br> &lt;/dl&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br> &lt;/div&gt;<br>&lt;/template&gt;<br>&lt;style&gt;<br> dt { font-weight: bold; }<br>&lt;/style&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="7a51" id="7a51" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;script&gt;<br>import axios from ‘axios’;<br>import moment from ‘moment’;</pre>
           <pre name="3d00" id="3d00" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">export default {<br> data(){<br>   return {<br>     orderDetails: false<br>   };<br> },<br> created(){<br>   var charge_id = this.$route.params.id;<br>   axios.get(`${window.endpoint}/charge/${charge_id}`)<br>      .then((res)=&gt;{<br>         this.orderDetails = res.data.charge;<br>       });<br> },<br> filters: {<br>   moment(date) {<br>     return moment.unix(date).format(‘MMMM Do, YYYY — h:mm a’);<br>   },<br>   currency(amount){<br>     return `$${(amount/100).toFixed( 2 )}`;<br>   }<br> }<br>}<br>&lt;/script&gt;</pre>
           <p name="8215" id="8215" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">In this file we hit our backend again to grab the details for the order from the identification number in the URL. We then bind that data to render on the screen using Vue.js. We also define moment and currency <a href="https://vuejs.org/v2/guide/migration.html#Filters" data-href="https://vuejs.org/v2/guide/migration.html#Filters" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">output filters </a>to format how the currency and dates are rendered to the screen.</p>
           <h4 name="0e98" id="0e98" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Testing the&nbsp;Frontend</h4>
           <p name="9bf0" id="9bf0" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">In your console run `npm run dev` and the frontend page of our website will be rendered out to <a href="http://localhost:8080/#/" data-href="http://localhost:8080/#/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">http://localhost:8080/#/</a> in a new tab. You should see the following screens for viewing the product and filling out order details.</p>
           <figure name="8991" id="8991" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 380px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 54.2%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*XURnk2WMjgpYyzIQWjq6Zw.png" data-width="1173" data-height="636" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*XURnk2WMjgpYyzIQWjq6Zw.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*XURnk2WMjgpYyzIQWjq6Zw.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*XURnk2WMjgpYyzIQWjq6Zw.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*XURnk2WMjgpYyzIQWjq6Zw.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figcaption class="imageCaption">
             Order Page
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
           <p name="be8e" id="be8e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">In the next section we will set up the Node.js server to create the actual charges.</p>
           <figure name="a4b9" id="a4b9" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 700px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 100%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*ncz6H8HUhnGUZcogbCuVMg.png" data-width="896" data-height="896" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*ncz6H8HUhnGUZcogbCuVMg.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*ncz6H8HUhnGUZcogbCuVMg.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*ncz6H8HUhnGUZcogbCuVMg.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*ncz6H8HUhnGUZcogbCuVMg.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figcaption class="imageCaption">
             Here is the source code repository for the frontend application code: 
             <a href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend" data-href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend" class="markup--anchor markup--figure-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener noopener" target="_blank">https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend</a>
            </figcaption>
           </figure>
           <p name="3716" id="3716" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Let’s set up the server!</p>
           <h3 name="ad56" id="ad56" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Backend Application</h3>
           <p name="310c" id="310c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Our server will be responsible for charging the user and providing the details about the order back to the customer. We are going to create a brand new project directory to keep our Node.js application. This will be a separate code repo from the frontend and deployed separately.</p>
           <p name="ee11" id="ee11" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">First let’s create our Node.js server projec and check the project into Git for version control. We will use git later on in order to deploy our app to the internet with Heroku.</p>
           <pre name="128a" id="128a" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ mkdir stickly-backend<br>$ cd stickly-backend<br>$ npm init<br>$ touch server.js .env .gitignore<br>$ git init<br>$ git add -A<br>$ git commit -m ‘initial commit’</pre>
           <p name="021a" id="021a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">This will set up an empty skeleton for our Node.js project and check the changes into git for version control. Make sure to add a `.gitignore` file that includes `.env` so that you do not accidentally push your secret keys to the internet. That file looks like this:</p>
           <p name="643c" id="643c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./.env</strong></p>
           <pre name="b030" id="b030" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_test_XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX</pre>
           <p name="42ff" id="42ff" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">There are a few npm packages that we need. These packages will be added to the *package.json* file due to the `?—?save` flag. The `npm init` command created our *package.json* file. To install additional Node.js packages with npm run:</p>
           <pre name="cccb" id="cccb" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ npm install express body-parser cors dotenv method-override stripe --save</pre>
           <p name="e4c4" id="e4c4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Most of these are helper packages that help the express Node.js web server accept and handle incoming requests from the internet. The Stripe package is for sending and processing payments.</p>
           <p name="0d27" id="0d27" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We’re going to define our application and routes in a <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">server.js</strong> file like so:</p>
           <p name="29a8" id="29a8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">./server.js</strong></p>
           <pre name="7db1" id="7db1" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">// Grabs our environment variables from the .env file<br>require(‘dotenv’).config();</pre>
           <pre name="5183" id="5183" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">var express = require(‘express’),<br> bodyParser = require(‘body-parser’),<br> methodOverride = require(‘method-override’),<br> cors = require(‘cors’),<br> app = express();</pre>
           <pre name="32da" id="32da" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Environment configuration<br>var env = process.env.NODE_ENV = process.env.NODE_ENV || ‘development’;<br>var port = process.env.PORT || 3000;</pre>
           <pre name="c006" id="c006" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Create a server side router<br>var router = express.Router();</pre>
           <pre name="2d3a" id="2d3a" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Configure express to handle HTTP requests<br>app.use(cors());<br>app.use(bodyParser.json());<br>app.use(bodyParser.urlencoded({<br> extended: true<br>})); <br>app.use(methodOverride());</pre>
           <pre name="f084" id="f084" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Configure our Stripe secret key and object<br>var stripe = require(‘stripe’)(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY);</pre>
           <pre name="3677" id="3677" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Define the route endpoints for our application</pre>
           <pre name="9863" id="9863" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Create a new charge<br>router.post(‘/charge’, function(req, res){<br> // Create the charge object with data from the Vue.js client<br> var newCharge = {<br>   amount: 23500,<br>   currency: “usd”,<br>   source: req.body.token_from_stripe, // obtained with Stripe.js on the client side<br>   description: req.body.specialNote,<br>   receipt_email: req.body.email,<br>   shipping: {<br>     name: req.body.name,<br>     address: {<br>       line1: req.body.address.street,<br>       city: req.body.address.city,<br>       state: req.body.address.state,<br>       postal_code: req.body.address.zip,<br>       country: ‘US’<br>     }<br>   }<br> };</pre>
           <pre name="6951" id="6951" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre"> // Call the stripe objects helper functions to trigger a new charge<br> stripe.charges.create(newCharge, function(err, charge) {<br>   // send response<br>   if (err){<br>     console.error(err);<br>     res.json({ error: err, charge: false });<br>   } else {<br>     // send response with charge data<br>     res.json({ error: false, charge: charge });<br>   }<br> });<br>});</pre>
           <pre name="fd31" id="fd31" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Route to get the data for a charge filtered by the charge’s id<br>router.get(‘/charge/:id’, function(req, res){<br> stripe.charges.retrieve(req.params.id, function(err, charge) {<br>   if (err){<br>     res.json({ error: err, charge: false });<br>   } else {<br>     res.json({ error: false, charge: charge });<br>   }<br> });<br>});</pre>
           <pre name="2d54" id="2d54" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Register the router<br>app.use(‘/’, router);</pre>
           <pre name="a044" id="a044" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// Start the server<br>app.listen(port, function(){<br> console.log(‘Server listening on port ‘ + port)<br>});</pre>
           <p name="1850" id="1850" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Congrats! We have our application set up in our local environment. To start the Vue application run `npm run dev` in the command line. Open a separate window and run `node server`. We can then trigger charges and navigate to the various web pages and hit the URL endpoints. In the next section we are going to deploy these applications to the internet.</p>
           <h3 name="bd68" id="bd68" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Deployment</h3>
           <p name="9d92" id="9d92" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Our frontend application is going to be hosted on Amazon S3. Our Node.js server will be hosted on Heroku.</p>
           <h4 name="947a" id="947a" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Deploy Vue.js app to&nbsp;S3</h4>
           <p name="a67f" id="a67f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">First, we are going to deploy our static website to Amazon Simple Storage Service (S3). If you are not familiar with S3 it is also possible to deploy to other static hosting services such as Github Pages or Netlify. S3 is very affordable and has the added benefit of scaling infinitely, in case A LOT of people want to buy sticks.</p>
           <p name="b3c6" id="b3c6" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Head into the AWS Consle and select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">S3</strong>. Once there, select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Create Bucket</strong>.</p>
           <figure name="276c" id="276c" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 627px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 89.60000000000001%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*H9iunPbUM9an7ga4yTOwHA.png" data-width="701" data-height="628" data-action="zoom" data-action-value="1*H9iunPbUM9an7ga4yTOwHA.png">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*H9iunPbUM9an7ga4yTOwHA.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*H9iunPbUM9an7ga4yTOwHA.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*H9iunPbUM9an7ga4yTOwHA.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="af40" id="af40" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">The bucket name must be globally unique so you will not be able to use the same bucket name as me. Since this server will be hosting our code we want it publicly accessible to everyone. Select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Grant public read access</strong>.</p>
           <figure name="5831" id="5831" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 626px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 89.4%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*p61KDWPyeg9vZmE2Z1iPfA.png" data-width="700" data-height="626">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*p61KDWPyeg9vZmE2Z1iPfA.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*p61KDWPyeg9vZmE2Z1iPfA.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*p61KDWPyeg9vZmE2Z1iPfA.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="c756" id="c756" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">After you created the bucket, click into it and select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Properties</strong> and then go to <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Static Website Hosting</strong>. This will serve up our <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">index.html</strong> file from the bucket’s unique URL.</p>
           <p name="0e85" id="0e85" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Congrats! You have set up an S3 bucket where we can host our website. To build our Vue.js app for production, head into the frontend repo and run:</p>
           <pre name="a4ae" id="a4ae" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ npm run build</pre>
           <p name="ca6d" id="ca6d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">This will generate a `dist` folder of our bundled Javascript files ready for production. We are going to then upload this folder and index.html to our S3 bucket. Go to your bucket and select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Upload</strong>. Drag and drop our Vue.js app into the bucket.</p>
           <figure name="0a97" id="0a97" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 700px; max-height: 627px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 89.60000000000001%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*LFYdrNBM6xUzFYYeepWFCw.png" data-width="700" data-height="627">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*LFYdrNBM6xUzFYYeepWFCw.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*LFYdrNBM6xUzFYYeepWFCw.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*LFYdrNBM6xUzFYYeepWFCw.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="9a45" id="9a45" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Click <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Next</strong>. On the following page, select <strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Grant public read access to this object(s)</strong>. Everything else can be kept as is.</p>
           <p name="09c1" id="09c1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Now if you head to <a href="http://YOUR_BUCKET_NAME.s3-website-REGION.amazonaws.com/#/" data-href="http://YOUR_BUCKET_NAME.s3-website-REGION.amazonaws.com/#/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">http://YOUR_BUCKET_NAME.s3-website-REGION.amazonaws.com/#/</a> you will be able to see your site live on the internet. For example, the link for my bucket is:</p>
           <p name="b0d5" id="b0d5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><a href="http://stickly.io.s3-website-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/#/" data-href="http://stickly.io.s3-website-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/#/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">http://stickly.io.s3-website-us-west-1.amazonaws.com/#/</a></p>
           <p name="fc52" id="fc52" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We will sort out a nicer domain name (optional step), but first, let’s deploy our server using Heroku.</p>
           <h4 name="6de8" id="6de8" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">Deploy Node.js app to&nbsp;Heroku</h4>
           <p name="2eb5" id="2eb5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">We need to add one file called a Procfile that tells Heroku how to start our server. It looks like this:</p>
           <p name="e2e4" id="e2e4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--p-strong">Procfile</strong></p>
           <pre name="3e61" id="3e61" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">web: node server.js</pre>
           <p name="cef1" id="cef1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Head into our server-side repo and make sure to install the heroku Command Line Interface (CLI). Check the project into git and create a new heroku application with the following commands:</p>
           <pre name="b4b7" id="b4b7" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ git init <br>$ git add -A<br>$ git commit -m ‘initial commit’<br>$ heroku create MY_APP_NAME</pre>
           <p name="ed5e" id="ed5e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">We also have to set our environment variables directly with Heroku. Run the following additional commands:</p>
           <pre name="d62b" id="d62b" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ heroku config:set STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_test_XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX</pre>
           <p name="7e8b" id="7e8b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">To deploy our server and view it in the browser run:</p>
           <pre name="99f9" id="99f9" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">$ git push heroku master<br>$ heroku open </pre>
           <p name="3a6d" id="3a6d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Our backend is live! Now when you navigate to the live frontend site our Vue.js app will call route functions on our Heroku server. Make sure that you update <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">src/main.js</em> environment configuration with you Heroku app name. This way in development we will make XHR (ajax) requests to localhost:3000 but in production requests go to our cloud server.</p>
           <p name="2261" id="2261" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">To accept real money you can update your Stripe environment variables with your production keys.</p>
           <p name="a82e" id="a82e" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Congrats on making it through this tutorial! You can view the source code for these applications below:</p>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="b35c" id="b35c" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Demo: </strong><a href="http://stickly.io/#/" data-href="http://stickly.io/#/" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">http://stickly.io/#/</a></li>
            <li name="3275" id="3275" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Frontend code:</strong> <a href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend" data-href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-frontend</a></li>
            <li name="e7b1" id="e7b1" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Backend code:</strong> <a href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-backend" data-href="https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-backend" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">https://github.com/connor11528/stickly-backend</a></li>
           </ul>
           <p name="781d" id="781d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li graf--trailing">Thanks for reading!</p>
          </div>
         </div>
